citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22" rel="nofollow">"Vasco da Gama"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Vasco+da+Gama%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2020</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gama_route_1.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="875" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gama_route_1.svg/300px-Gama_route_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gama_route_1.svg/450px-Gama_route_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gama_route_1.svg/600px-Gama_route_1.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gama_route_1.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The route followed in Vasco da Gama's first voyage (1497–1499)</div></div></div>
<p>On 8 July 1497 Vasco da Gama led a fleet of four ships<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundations_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-17">[17]</a></sup> with a crew of 170 men from <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>. The distance traveled in the journey around Africa to India and back was greater than the length of the equator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundations_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The navigators included Portugal's most experienced, Pero de Alenquer, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Escobar" title="Pedro Escobar">Pedro Escobar</a>, João de Coimbra, and Afonso Gonçalves. It is not known for certain how many people were in each ship's crew but approximately 55 returned, and two ships were lost. Two of the vessels were <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carracks</a>, newly built for the voyage; the others were a <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravel</a> and a supply boat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundations_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The four ships were:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Gabriel_(ship)" title="São Gabriel (ship)">São Gabriel</a></i>, commanded by Vasco da Gama; a <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a> of 178 tons, length 27 m, width 8.5 m, <a href="/wiki/Draft_(hull)" title="Draft (hull)">draft</a> 2.3 m, sails of 372 m<sup>2</sup></li>
<li><i>São Rafael</i>, commanded by his brother <a href="/wiki/Paulo_da_Gama" title="Paulo da Gama">Paulo da Gama</a>; similar dimensions to the <i>São Gabriel</i></li>
<li><i>Berrio</i> (nickname, officially called <i>São Miguel</i>), a caravel, slightly smaller than the former two, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Nicolau_Coelho" title="Nicolau Coelho">Nicolau Coelho</a></li>
<li>A storage ship of unknown name, commanded by Gonçalo Nunes, destined to be scuttled in <a href="/wiki/Mossel_Bay" title="Mossel Bay">Mossel Bay</a> (São Brás) in South Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ames_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-ames-8">[8]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Journey_to_the_Cape">Journey to the Cape</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cross_daGama2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="318" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cross_daGama2.jpg/220px-Cross_daGama2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cross_daGama2.jpg/330px-Cross_daGama2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cross_daGama2.jpg/440px-Cross_daGama2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cross_daGama2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to the Cross of Vasco da Gama at the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, South Africa</div></div></div>
<p>The expedition set sail from Lisbon on 8 July 1497. It followed the route pioneered by earlier explorers along the coast of Africa via <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> Islands. After reaching the coast of present-day <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, da Gama took a course south into the open ocean, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a> and seeking the South Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">westerlies</a> that <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> had discovered in 1487.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This course proved successful and on 4 November 1497, the expedition made landfall on the African coast. For over three months the ships had sailed more than 10,000 kilometres (6,000 mi) of open ocean, by far the longest journey out of sight of land made by that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundations_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 16 December, the fleet had passed the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fish_River" title="Great Fish River">Great Fish River</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape" title="Eastern Cape">Eastern Cape</a>, South Africa) – where Dias had anchored – and sailed into waters previously unknown to Europeans. With Christmas pending, da Gama and his crew gave the coast they were passing the name <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal_Province" title="KwaZulu-Natal Province">Natal</a>, which carried the connotation of "birth of Christ" in Portuguese.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozambique">Mozambique</span></h3>
<p>Vasco da Gama spent 2 to 29 March 1498 in the vicinity of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozambique_Island" title="Mozambique Island">Mozambique Island</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a>-controlled territory on the East African coast was an integral part of the network of trade in the Indian Ocean. Fearing the local population would be hostile to Christians, da Gama impersonated a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> and gained audience with the Sultan of <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. With the paltry trade goods he had to offer, the explorer was unable to provide a suitable gift to the ruler. Soon the local populace became suspicious of da Gama and his men. Forced by a hostile crowd to flee Mozambique, da Gama departed the harbor, firing his cannons into the city in retaliation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mombasa">Mombasa</span></h3>
<p>In the vicinity of modern <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, the expedition resorted to <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a>, looting Arab merchant ships that were generally unarmed trading vessels without heavy cannons. The Portuguese became the first known Europeans to visit the port of <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> from 7 to 13 April 1498, but were met with hostility and soon departed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malindi">Malindi</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1488" data-file-width="1984" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg/220px-Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg/330px-Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg/440px-Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pillar_of_Vasco_da_Gama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pillar of Vasco da Gama in <a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a>, in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, erected on the return journey</div></div></div>
<p>Vasco da Gama continued north, arriving on 14 April 1498 at the friendlier port of <a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a>, whose leaders were having a conflict with those of <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>. There the expedition first noted evidence of Indian traders. Da Gama and his crew contracted the services of a pilot who used his knowledge of the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> winds to guide the expedition the rest of the way to <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Calicut</a>, located on the southwest coast of India. Sources differ over the identity of the pilot, calling him variously a Christian, a Muslim, and a <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_people" title="Gujarati people">Gujarati</a>. One traditional story describes the pilot as the famous Arab navigator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Majid" title="Ibn Majid">Ibn Majid</a>, but other contemporaneous accounts place Majid elsewhere, and he could not have been near the vicinity at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> None of the Portuguese historians of the time mentions Ibn Majid. Vasco da Gama left Malindi for India on 24 April 1498.
</p>
<h3><span id="Calicut.2C_India"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Calicut,_India">Calicut, India</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="1221" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg/220px-A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg/330px-A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg/440px-A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_chegada_de_Vasco_da_Gama_a_Calicute_em_1498.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The arrival of Vasco da Gama at Calicut, by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roque_Gameiro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roque Gameiro (page does not exist)">Roque Gameiro</a>, 1900.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1286" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png/220px-Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png/330px-Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png/440px-Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_perante_o_Samorim_de_Calecute.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vasco da Gama before the <a href="/wiki/Zamorin" title="Zamorin">Zamorin</a> of Calicut, by <a href="/wiki/Veloso_Salgado" title="Veloso Salgado">Veloso Salgado</a>, 1898.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg/220px-Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg/330px-Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg/440px-Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_Memo_Kappad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landmark in Kappad, near <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Calicut</a></div></div></div>
<p>The fleet arrived in <a href="/wiki/Kappad" title="Kappad">Kappadu</a> near Kozhikode (Calicut), in <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> (present day <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a> state of India), on 20 May 1498. The King of Calicut, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saamoothiri" title="Saamoothiri">Samudiri</a> (Zamorin), who was at that time staying in his second capital at <a href="/wiki/Ponnani" title="Ponnani">Ponnani</a>, returned to Calicut on hearing the news of the foreign fleet's arrival. The navigator was received with traditional hospitality, including a grand procession of at least 3,000 armed <a href="/wiki/Nair" title="Nair">Nairs</a>, but an interview with the Zamorin failed to produce any concrete results. When local authorities asked da Gama's fleet, "What brought you hither?", they replied that they had come "in search of Christians and spices."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The presents that da Gama sent to the Zamorin as gifts from Dom Manuel – four cloaks of scarlet cloth, six hats, four branches of corals, twelve <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">almasares</i></span>, a box with seven brass vessels, a chest of sugar, two barrels of oil and a cask of honey – were trivial, and failed to impress. While Zamorin's officials wondered at why there was no gold or silver, the Muslim merchants who considered da Gama their rival suggested that the latter was only an ordinary pirate and not a royal ambassador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Vasco da Gama's request for permission to leave a factor behind him in charge of the merchandise he could not sell was turned down by the King, who insisted that da Gama pay customs duty – preferably in gold – like any other trader, which strained the relation between the two. Annoyed by this, da Gama carried a few Nairs and sixteen fishermen (mukkuva) off with him by force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return">Return</span></h3>
<p>Vasco da Gama left Calicut on 29 August 1498. Eager to set sail for home, he ignored the local knowledge of monsoon wind patterns that were still blowing onshore. The fleet initially inched north along the Indian coast, and then anchored in at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anjediva" title="Anjediva">Anjediva</a> island for a spell. They finally struck out for their Indian Ocean crossing on 3 October 1498. But with the winter monsoon yet to set in, it was a harrowing journey. On the outgoing journey, sailing with the summer monsoon wind, da Gama's fleet crossed the Indian Ocean in only 23 days; now, on the return trip, sailing against the wind, it took 132 days.
</p><p>Da Gama saw land again only on 2 January 1499, passing before the coastal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_people" title="Somali people">Somali</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>, then under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Ajuran_Sultanate" title="Ajuran Sultanate">Ajuran Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>. The fleet did not make a stop, but passing before Mogadishu, the anonymous diarist of the expedition noted that it was a large city with houses of four or five storeys high and big palaces in its center and many mosques with cylindrical minarets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Da Gama's fleet finally arrived in Malindi on 7 January 1499, in a terrible state – approximately half of the crew had died during the crossing, and many of the rest were afflicted with <a href="/wiki/Scurvy" title="Scurvy">scurvy</a>. Not having enough crewmen left standing to manage three ships, da Gama ordered the <i>São Rafael</i> scuttled off the East African coast, and the crew re-distributed to the remaining two ships, the <i>São Gabriel</i> and the <i>Berrio</i>. Thereafter, the sailing was smoother. By early March, they had arrived in Mossel Bay, and crossed the Cape of Good Hope in the opposite direction on 20 March, reaching the west African coast by 25 April.
</p><p>The diary record of the expedition ends abruptly here. Reconstructing from other sources, it seems they continued to Cape Verde, where Nicolau Coelho's <i>Berrio</i> separated from Vasco da Gama's <i>São Gabriel</i> and sailed on by itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The <i>Berrio</i> arrived in Lisbon on 10 July 1499 and <a href="/wiki/Nicolau_Coelho" title="Nicolau Coelho">Nicolau Coelho</a> personally delivered the news to King Manuel I and the royal court, then assembled in <a href="/wiki/Sintra" title="Sintra">Sintra</a>. In the meantime, back in Cape Verde, da Gama's brother, Paulo da Gama, had fallen grievously ill. Da Gama elected to stay by his side on <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a> island and handed the <i>São Gabriel</i> over to his clerk, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A1" title="João de Sá">João de Sá</a>, to take home. The <i>São Gabriel</i> under Sá arrived in Lisbon sometime in late July or early August. Da Gama and his sickly brother eventually hitched a ride with a Guinea caravel returning to Portugal, but Paulo da Gama died en route. Da Gama disembarked at the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> to bury his brother at the monastery of São Francisco in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angra_do_Heroismo" title="Angra do Heroismo">Angra do Heroismo</a>, and lingered there for a little while in mourning. He eventually took passage on an Azorean caravel and finally arrived in Lisbon on 29 August 1499 (according to Barros),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> or early September<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundations_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-17">[17]</a></sup> (8th or 18th, according to other sources). Despite his melancholic mood, da Gama was given a hero's welcome and showered with honors, including a triumphal procession and public festivities. King Manuel wrote two letters in which he described da Gama's first voyage, in July and August 1499, soon after the return of the ships. <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Sernigi" title="Girolamo Sernigi">Girolamo Sernigi</a> also wrote three letters describing da Gama's first voyage soon after the return of the expedition.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="1047" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif/350px-Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif/525px-Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif/700px-Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Portuguese_Carreira_da_India.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outward and return voyages of the Portuguese India Run (<i>Carreira da Índia</i>). The outward route of the South Atlantic westerlies that Bartolomeu Dias discovered in 1487, followed and explored by da Gama in the open ocean, would be developed in subsequent years.</div></div></div>
<p>The expedition had exacted a large cost – two ships and over half the men had been lost. It had also failed in its principal mission of securing a commercial treaty with Calicut. Nonetheless, the small quantities of spices and other trade goods brought back on the remaining two ships demonstrated the potential of great profit for future trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Vasco da Gama was justly celebrated for opening a direct sea route to Asia. His path would be followed up thereafter by yearly <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">Portuguese India Armadas</a>.
</p><p>The spice trade would prove to be a major asset to the Portuguese royal treasury, and other consequences soon followed. For example, da Gama's voyage had made it clear that the east coast of Africa, the <i>Contra Costa</i>, was essential to Portuguese interests; its ports provided fresh water, provisions, timber, and harbors for repairs, and served as a refuge where ships could wait out unfavorable weather. One significant result was the colonization of <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> by the Portuguese Crown.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rewards">Rewards</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="220" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg/220px-Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg/330px-Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg/440px-Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_signature_almirante.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vasco da Gama's signature (reads Ho Comde Almirante, "The Count Admiral")</div></div></div>
<p>In December 1499, King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> rewarded Vasco da Gama with the town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sines_Municipality" title="Sines Municipality">Sines</a> as a hereditary fief (the town his father, <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_da_Gama_(15th_century)" title="Estêvão da Gama (15th century)">Estêvão</a>, had once held as a <i>commenda</i>). This turned out to be a complicated affair, for Sines still belonged to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_James_of_the_Sword" title="Order of Saint James of the Sword">Order of Santiago</a>. The master of the Order, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jorge_de_Lencastre" title="Jorge de Lencastre">Jorge de Lencastre</a>, might have endorsed the reward – after all, da Gama was a Santiago knight, one of their own, and a close associate of Lencastre himself. But the fact that Sines was awarded by the king provoked Lencastre to refuse out of principle, lest it encourage the king to make other donations of the Order's properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Da Gama would spend the next few years attempting to take hold of Sines, an effort that would estrange him from Lencastre and eventually prompt da Gama to abandon his beloved Order of Santiago, switching over to the rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Christ_(Portugal)" title="Order of Christ (Portugal)">Order of Christ</a> in 1507.
</p><p>In the meantime, da Gama made do with a substantial hereditary royal pension of 300,000 <i><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_real" title="Portuguese real">reis</a></i>. He was awarded the noble title of <i>Dom</i> (<a href="/wiki/Lord" title="Lord">lord</a>) in perpetuity for himself, his siblings and their descendants. On 30 January 1502, da Gama was awarded the title of <i>Almirante dos mares de Arabia, Persia, India e de todo o Oriente</i> ("Admiral of the Seas of Arabia, Persia, India and all the Orient") – an overwrought title reminiscent of the ornate Castilian title borne by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> (evidently, Manuel must have reckoned that if <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> had an 'Admiral of the Ocean Seas', then surely Portugal should have one too).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Another royal letter, dated October 1501, gave da Gama the personal right to intervene and exercise a determining role on <i>any</i> future India-bound fleet.
</p><p>Around 1501, Vasco da Gama married Catarina de Ataíde, daughter of Álvaro de Ataíde, the <i><a href="/wiki/Alcaide" title="Alcaide">alcaide-mór</a></i> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alvor_Parish" title="Alvor Parish">Alvor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>), and a prominent nobleman connected by kinship with the powerful <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Abrantes" title="Count of Abrantes">Almeida</a> family (Catarina was a first cousin of <a href="/wiki/Don_(honorific)" title="Don (honorific)">Dom</a> <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Francisco de Almeida</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_voyage">Second voyage</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/4th_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Gama,_1502)" title="4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)">4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vasco_da_Gama&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2020</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gama_armada_in_India,_1502.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="349" decoding="async" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Gama_armada_in_India%2C_1502.gif/220px-Gama_armada_in_India%2C_1502.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Gama_armada_in_India%2C_1502.gif/330px-Gama_armada_in_India%2C_1502.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Gama_armada_in_India%2C_1502.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gama_armada_in_India,_1502.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> of India, c. 1500, showing the path of Vasco da Gama's <a href="/wiki/4th_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Gama,_1502)" title="4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)">4th India Armada</a> in 1502</div></div></div>
<p>The follow-up expedition, the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Cabral,_1500)" title="2nd Portuguese India Armada (Cabral, 1500)">Second India Armada</a>, launched in 1500 under the command of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a> with the mission of making a treaty with the <a href="/wiki/Zamorin" title="Zamorin">Zamorin</a> of Calicut and setting up a Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factory</a> in the city. However, Pedro Cabral entered into a conflict with the local Arab merchant guilds, with the result that the Portuguese factory was overrun in a riot and up to 70 Portuguese were killed. Cabral blamed the Zamorin for the incident and bombarded the city. Thus war broke out between Portugal and Calicut.
</p><p>Vasco da Gama invoked his royal letter to take command of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Gama,_1502)" title="4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)">4th India Armada</a>, scheduled to set out in 1502, with the explicit aim of taking revenge upon the Zamorin and force him to submit to Portuguese terms. The heavily armed fleet of fifteen ships and eight hundred men left Lisbon on 12 February 1502. It was followed in April by another squadron of five ships led by his cousin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_da_Gama_(c.1470)" title="Estêvão da Gama (c.1470)">Estêvão da Gama</a> (the son of Aires da Gama), which caught up to them in the Indian Ocean. The 4th Armada was a veritable da Gama family affair. Two of his maternal uncles, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Sodr%C3%A9" title="Vicente Sodré">Vicente Sodré</a> and Brás Sodré, were pre-designated to command an Indian Ocean naval patrol, while brothers-in-law Álvaro de Ataíde (brother of Vasco's wife Catarina) and Lopo Mendes de Vasconcelos (betrothed to Teresa da Gama, Vasco's sister) captained ships in the main fleet.
</p><p>On the outgoing voyage, da Gama's fleet opened contact with the East African gold trading port of <a href="/wiki/Sofala" title="Sofala">Sofala</a> and reduced the sultanate of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilwa" title="Kilwa">Kilwa</a> to tribute, extracting a substantial sum of gold.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pilgrim_ship_incident">Pilgrim ship incident</span></h3>
<p>On reaching India in October 1502, da Gama's fleet intercepted <i>Mirim</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-33">[33]</a></sup> a ship of Muslim pilgrims at <a href="/wiki/Madayi" title="Madayi">Madayi</a> travelling from Calicut to Mecca. Described in detail by eyewitness <a href="/wiki/Thom%C3%A9_Lopes" title="Thomé Lopes">Thomé Lopes</a> and chronicler <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Correia" title="Gaspar Correia">Gaspar Correia</a>, da Gama looted the ship with over 400 pilgrims on board including 50 women, locked in the passengers, the owner and an ambassador from Egypt and burned them to death. They offered their wealth, which "could ransom all the Christian slaves in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Fez" title="Kingdom of Fez">Kingdom of Fez</a> and much more" but were not spared. Da Gama looked on through the porthole and saw the women bringing up their gold and jewels and holding up their babies to beg for mercy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The lives of twenty children were spared against a forced conversion to Christianity<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calicut">Calicut</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gama_squadron_of_1502_Armada_(Livro_das_Armadas).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="280" decoding="async" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Gama_squadron_of_1502_Armada_%28Livro_das_Armadas%29.jpg/220px-Gama_squadron_of_1502_Armada_%28Livro_das_Armadas%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Gama_squadron_of_1502_Armada_%28Livro_das_Armadas%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gama_squadron_of_1502_Armada_(Livro_das_Armadas).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A depiction of da Gama's fleet (from the <i>Livro das Armadas</i>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_(Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="553" decoding="async" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/200px-Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/300px-Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/400px-Vasco_da_Gama_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_(Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aged Vasco da Gama, as Viceroy of India and Count of Vidigueira (from <i>Livro de Lisuarte de Abreu</i>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St-Francis-Church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="225" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/St-Francis-Church.jpg/220px-St-Francis-Church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/St-Francis-Church.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St-Francis-Church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. Francis CSI Church, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochin" title="Cochin">Kochi</a>. Vasco da Gama died in Kochi in 1524 when he was on his third visit to India. His body was originally buried in this church.</div></div></div>
<p>After stopping at Cannanore, Gama drove his fleet before Calicut, demanding redress for the treatment of Cabral. Having known of the fate of the pilgrims' ship, the Zamorin adopted a conciliatory attitude towards the Portuguese and expressed willingness to sign a new treaty but da Gama made a call to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> king to expel all Muslims from Calicut before beginning negotiations, which was turned down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> At the same time however, the Zamorin sent a message to his rebellious vassal, the Raja of Cochin urging cooperation and obedience to counter the Portuguese threat; the ruler of Cochin forwarded this message to Gama, which reinforced his opinion of the Indians as duplicitous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> After demanding the expulsion of Muslims from Calicut to the Hindu Zamorin, the latter sent the high priest Talappana <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namboothiri" title="Namboothiri">Namboothiri</a> (the very same person who conducted da Gama to the Zamorin's chamber during his much celebrated first visit to Calicut in May 1498) for talks. Da Gama called him a spy, ordered the priest's lips and ears to be cut off and after sewing a pair of dog's ears to his head, sent him away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.G.S._Narayanan,_Calicut_2006_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-M.G.S._Narayanan,_Calicut_2006-37">[37]</a></sup> The Portuguese fleet then bombarded the unfortified city for nearly two days from the sea, severely damaging it. He also captured several rice vessels and cut off the crew's hands, ears and noses, dispatching them with a note to the Zamorin, in which Gama declared that he would be open to friendly relations once the Zamorin had paid for the items plundered from the feitoria as well as the gunpowder and cannonballs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seabattle">Seabattle</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Calicut_(1503)" title="Battle of Calicut (1503)">Battle of Calicut (1503)</a></div>
<p>The violent treatment meted out by da Gama quickly brought trade along the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> of India, upon which Calicut depended, to a standstill. The Zamorin ventured to dispatch a fleet of strong warships to challenge da Gama's armada, but which Gama managed to defeat <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Calicut_(1503)" title="Battle of Calicut (1503)">in a naval battle before Calicut harbor</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cochin">Cochin</span></h3>
<p>Da Gama loaded up with spices at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochin" title="Cochin">Cochin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannanore" title="Cannanore">Cannanore</a>, small nearby kingdoms at war with the Zamorin, whose alliances had been secured by prior Portuguese fleets. The 4th armada left India in early 1503. Da Gama left behind a small squadron of caravels under the command of his uncle, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Sodr%C3%A9" title="Vicente Sodré">Vicente Sodré</a>, to patrol the Indian coast, to continue harassing Calicut shipping, and to protect the Portuguese factories at Cochin and Cannanore from the Zamorin's inevitable reprisals.
</p><p>Vasco da Gama arrived back in Portugal in September 1503, effectively having failed in his mission to bring the Zamorin to submission. This failure, and the subsequent more galling failure of his uncle Vicente Sodré to protect the Portuguese factory in Cochin, probably counted against any further rewards. When the Portuguese king <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> decided to appoint the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">governor and viceroy</a> of Portuguese India in 1505, da Gama was conspicuously overlooked, and the post given to <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Francisco de Almeida</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interlude">Interlude</span></h2>
<p>For the next two decades, Vasco da Gama lived out a quiet life, unwelcome in the royal court and sidelined from Indian affairs. His attempts to return to the favor of Manuel I (including switching over to the Order of Christ in 1507), yielded little. <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Almeida</a>, the larger-than-life <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> and, later on, <a href="/wiki/Lopo_Soares_de_Albergaria" title="Lopo Soares de Albergaria">Albergaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Lopes_de_Sequeira" title="Diogo Lopes de Sequeira">Sequeira</a>, were the king's preferred point men for India.
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> defected to the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> in 1518, Vasco da Gama threatened to do the same, prompting the king to undertake steps to retain him in Portugal and avoid the embarrassment of losing his own "Admiral of the Indies" to Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1519, after years of ignoring his petitions, King Manuel I finally hurried to give Vasco da Gama a feudal title, appointing him the first <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Vidigueira" title="Count of Vidigueira">Count of Vidigueira</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Count" title="Count">count</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Title_of_nobility" title="Title of nobility">title</a> created by a royal decree issued in Évora on 29 December, after a complicated agreement with Dom <a href="/wiki/Jaime,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Jaime, Duke of Braganza">Jaime, Duke of Braganza</a>, who ceded him on payment the towns of <a href="/wiki/Vidigueira" title="Vidigueira">Vidigueira</a> and Vila dos Frades. The decree granted Vasco da Gama and his heirs all the revenues and privileges related,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> thus establishing da Gama as the first Portuguese count who was not born with royal blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_voyage_and_death">Third voyage and death</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4982" data-file-width="2949" decoding="async" height="372" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg/220px-Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg/330px-Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg/440px-Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kochi_2018-04-04g.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gama's former tomb in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Francis_Church,_Kochi" title="St. Francis Church, Kochi">St. Francis Church, Kochi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:176px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Francis_Church,_Fort_Kochi_001_(17).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1456" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg/174px-St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg/262px-St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg/349px-St_Francis_Church%2C_Fort_Kochi_001_%2817%29.jpg 2x" width="174"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St_Francis_Church,_Fort_Kochi_001_(17).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque engraved near the tomb in St Francis's Church</div></div></div>
<p>After the death of King Manuel I in late 1521, his son and successor, King <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III of Portugal</a> set about reviewing the Portuguese government overseas. Turning away from the old Albuquerque clique (now represented by <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Lopes_de_Sequeira" title="Diogo Lopes de Sequeira">Diogo Lopes de Sequeira</a>), John III looked for a fresh start. Vasco da Gama re-emerged from his political wilderness as an important adviser to the new king's appointments and strategy. Seeing the new Spanish threat to the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a> as the priority, Vasco da Gama advised against the obsession with Arabia that had pervaded much of the Manueline period, and continued to be the dominant concern of <a href="/wiki/Duarte_de_Menezes" title="Duarte de Menezes">Duarte de Menezes</a>, then-<a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">governor of Portuguese India</a>. Menezes also turned out to be incompetent and corrupt, subject to numerous complaints. As a result, John III decided to appoint Vasco da Gama himself to replace Menezes, confident that the magic of his name and memory of his deeds might better impress his authority on Portuguese India, and manage the transition to a new government and new strategy.
</p><p>By his appointment letter of February 1524, John III granted Vasco da Gama the privileged title of "<a href="/wiki/Viceroy#Portuguese_Empire" title="Viceroy">Viceroy</a>", being only the second Portuguese governor to enjoy that title (the first was <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Francisco de Almeida</a> in 1505).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> His second son, <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_da_Gama_(16th_century)" title="Estêvão da Gama (16th century)">Estêvão da Gama</a> was simultaneously appointed <i>Capitão-mor do Mar da Índia</i> ('Captain-major of the Indian Sea', commander of the Indian Ocean naval patrol fleet), to replace Duarte's brother, Luís de Menezes. As a final condition, Gama secured from <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III of Portugal</a> the commitment to appoint all his sons successively as Portuguese captains of <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>.
</p><p>Setting out in April 1524, with a fleet of fourteen ships, Vasco da Gama took as his flagship the famous large carrack <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_do_Monte_Sinai" title="Santa Catarina do Monte Sinai">Santa Catarina do Monte Sinai</a></i> on her last journey to India, along with two of his sons, Estêvão and Paulo. After a troubled journey<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Please give a basic description of the route. (April 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (four or five of the ships were lost en route), he arrived in India in September. Vasco da Gama immediately invoked his high viceregent powers to impose a new order in Portuguese India, replacing all the old officials with his own appointments. But Gama contracted <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> not long after arriving, and died in the city of Cochin on Christmas Eve in 1524, three months after his arrival. As per royal instructions, da Gama was succeeded as governor of India by one of the captains who had come with him, Henrique de Menezes (no relation to Duarte). Da Gama's sons Estêvão and Paulo immediately lost their posts and joined the returning fleet of early 1525 (along with the dismissed Duarte de Menezes and Luís de Menezes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>Vasco da Gama's body was first buried at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Francis_Church,_Cochin" title="St. Francis Church, Cochin">St. Francis Church</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Kochi" title="Fort Kochi">Fort Kochi</a> in the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kochi_(India)" title="Kochi (India)">Kochi</a>, but his remains were returned to Portugal in 1539. The body of Vasco da Gama was re-interred in Vidigueira in a casket decorated with gold and jewels.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:33630-Lisbon_(36358426111).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2003" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg/220px-33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg/330px-33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg/440px-33630-Lisbon_%2836358426111%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:33630-Lisbon_(36358426111).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tomb of Vasco da Gama in the <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery" title="Jerónimos Monastery">Jerónimos Monastery</a> in Belém, Lisbon</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery,_Lisbon" title="Jerónimos Monastery, Lisbon">Monastery of the Hieronymites</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m,_Lisbon" title="Belém, Lisbon">Belém</a>, which would become the necropolis of the Portuguese royal dynasty of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">Aviz</a>, was erected in the early 1500s near the launch point of Vasco da Gama's first journey, and its construction funded by a tax on the profits of the yearly Portuguese India Armadas. In 1880, da Gama's remains and those of the poet <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Luís de Camões">Luís de Camões</a> (who celebrated da Gama's first voyage in his 1572 epic poem, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Lusiad" title="The Lusiad">The Lusiad</a></i>), were moved to new carved tombs in the nave of the monastery's church, only a few meters away from the tombs of the kings <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III</a>, whom da Gama had served.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_descendants">Marriage and descendants</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="1642" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png/220px-Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png/330px-Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png/440px-Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_o_navegador_escudo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coat of arms of Vasco da Gama.</div></div></div>
<p>Vasco da Gama and his wife, Catarina de <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ata%C3%ADde_(fam%C3%ADlia)" title="pt:Ataíde (família)">Ataíde</a>, had six sons and one daughter:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Dom Francisco da Gama, who inherited his father's titles as 2nd <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Vidigueira" title="Count of Vidigueira">Count of Vidigueira</a> and the 2nd "Admiral of the Seas of India, Arabia and Persia". He remained in Portugal.</li>
<li>Dom <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_da_Gama_(16th_century)" title="Estêvão da Gama (16th century)">Estevão da Gama</a>, after his abortive 1524 term as Indian patrol captain, he was appointed for a three-year term as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Malacca#Portuguese_administration_of_Malacca" title="Portuguese Malacca"><i>captain of Malacca</i></a>, serving from 1534 to 1539 (includes the last two years of his younger brother Paulo's term). He was subsequently appointed as the 11th <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">governor of India</a> from 1540 to 1542.</li>
<li>Dom Paulo da Gama (having the same name as his uncle <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paulo_da_Gama" title="pt:Paulo da Gama">Paulo</a>), captain of Malacca from 1533 to 1534, killed in a naval action off <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>.</li>
<li>Dom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cristov%C3%A3o_da_Gama" title="Cristovão da Gama">Cristovão da Gama</a>, captain of Malacca from 1538 to 1540; nominated to succeed in Malacca, but executed by <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Ibrahim_al-Ghazi" title="Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Ghazi">Ahmad ibn Ibrahim</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethiopian-Adal_war" title="Ethiopian-Adal war">Ethiopian-Adal war</a> in 1542.</li>
<li>Dom Pedro da Silva da Gama, appointed captain of Malacca from 1548 to 1552.</li>
<li>Dom Álvaro de Ataíde da Gama, appointed captain of Malacca fleet in the 1540s, captain of Malacca itself from 1552 to 1554.</li>
<li>Dona Isabel de Ataíde da Gama, only daughter, married Dom Ignacio de Noronha, son of the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_of_Linhares" title="Count of Linhares">Count of Linhares</a>.</li></ol>
<p>His male-line issue became extinct in 1735, when the 7th Count of Vidigueira, Dom Vasco Baltasar José Luís Gama died, leaving only one daughter from his marriage, Dona Maria José da Gama, who inherited the Vidigueira estate. The title thus continued through this female-line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intergenerations">Intergenerations</span></h3>
<ul><li>Dom <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama,_3.%C2%BA_Conde_da_Vidigueira" title="pt:Vasco da Gama, 3.º Conde da Vidigueira">Vasco da Gama, 3rd Count of Vidigueira</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_personnel" title="Military personnel">military personnel</a>, son of Francisco (2nd Count) and grandson of Vasco da Gama.</li>
<li>Dom <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_da_Gama,_4.%C2%BA_Conde_da_Vidigueira" title="pt:Francisco da Gama, 4.º Conde da Vidigueira">Francisco da Gama, 4th Count of Vidigueira</a>, the viceroy (1597–1600) and governor (1622–1628) of India, son of Vasco (3rd Count) and great-grandson of Vasco da Gama.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1754" data-file-width="1275" decoding="async" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png/220px-Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png/330px-Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png/440px-Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vasco_da_Gama_-_1838.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of Vasco da Gama by <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Manuel_da_Fonseca" title="António Manuel da Fonseca">António Manuel da Fonseca</a> (1838)</div></div></div>
<p>Vasco da Gama is one of the most famous and celebrated explorers from the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. As much as anyone after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, he was responsible for Portugal's success as an early colonising power. Beside the fact of the first voyage itself, it was his astute mix of politics and war on the other side of the world that placed Portugal in a prominent position in <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_trade" title="Indian Ocean trade">Indian Ocean trade</a>. Following da Gama's initial voyage, the Portuguese crown realized that securing outposts on the eastern coast of Africa would prove vital to maintaining national trade routes to the Far East.
</p><p>However, his fame is tempered by such incidents and attitudes as displayed in the notorious Pilgrim Ship Incident previously discussed.
</p><p>The Portuguese <a href="/wiki/National_epic" title="National epic">national epic</a>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lus%C3%ADadas" title="Lusíadas">Lusíadas</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Luís de Camões">Luís Vaz de Camões</a>, largely concerns Vasco da Gama's voyages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1865 <a href="/wiki/Grand_opera" title="Grand opera">grand opera</a> <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Africaine" title="L'Africaine">L'Africaine</a>: Opéra en Cinq Actes</i>, composed by <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Meyerbeer" title="Giacomo Meyerbeer">Giacomo Meyerbeer</a> from a libretto by <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Scribe" title="Eugène Scribe">Eugène Scribe</a>, prominently includes the character of Vasco da Gama. The events depicted, however, are fictitious. Meyerbeer's working title for the opera was <i>Vasco da Gama</i>. A 1989 production of the opera by the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Opera" title="San Francisco Opera">San Francisco Opera</a> featured noted <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plácido Domingo">Plácido Domingo</a> in the role of da Gama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The 19th-century composer <a href="/wiki/Louis-Albert_Bourgault-Ducoudray" title="Louis-Albert Bourgault-Ducoudray">Louis-Albert Bourgault-Ducoudray</a> composed an eponymous 1872 opera based on da Gama's life and exploits at sea.
</p><p>The port city of <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama,_Goa" title="Vasco da Gama, Goa">Vasco da Gama</a> in Goa is named after him, as is the crater <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_(crater)" title="Vasco da Gama (crater)">Vasco da Gama</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>. There are three football clubs in Brazil (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_de_Regatas_Vasco_da_Gama" title="Club de Regatas Vasco da Gama">Club de Regatas Vasco da Gama</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasco_Sports_Club" title="Vasco Sports Club">Vasco Sports Club</a> in Goa that were also named after him. There exists a church in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kochi_(India)" title="Kochi (India)">Kochi</a>, Kerala called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Church" title="Vasco da Gama Church">Vasco da Gama Church</a>, and a private residence on the island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a>. The suburb of Vasco in Cape Town also honours him.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_(49219762623).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg/220px-Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg/330px-Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg/440px-Lisbon_%2849219762623%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_(49219762623).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cenotaph to Vasco da Gama in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Santa_Engr%C3%A1cia" title="Church of Santa Engrácia">Church of Santa Engrácia</a>, now the National Pantheon in Lisbon.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama,_1969.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg/220px-50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg/330px-50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg/440px-50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama%2C_1969.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:50_Escudos_c%C3%A9l%C3%A9brant_le_500e_anniversaire_de_la_naissance_de_Vasco_Da_Gama,_1969.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portuguese coin from 1969 commemorating the 500th anniversary of Vasco da Gama's birth.</div></div></div>
<p>A few places in Lisbon's <a href="/wiki/Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es" title="Parque das Nações">Parque das Nações</a> are named after the explorer, such as the <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Bridge" title="Vasco da Gama Bridge">Vasco da Gama Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Tower" title="Vasco da Gama Tower">Vasco da Gama Tower</a> and the <i>Centro Comercial Vasco da Gama</i> shopping centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Oceanarium" title="Lisbon Oceanarium">Oceanário</a> in the Parque das Nações has a mascot of a cartoon diver with the name of "Vasco", who is named after the explorer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>Vasco da Gama was the only explorer on the final pool of <a href="/wiki/Os_Grandes_Portugueses" title="Os Grandes Portugueses">Os Grandes Portugueses</a>. Although the final shortlist featured other <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> related people, they were not actually explorers nor navigators for any matter.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Portuguese Navy</a> has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_class_frigate" title="Vasco da Gama class frigate">class of frigates</a> named after him. There are three <i>Vasco da Gama</i> class frigates in total, of which the first one also <a href="/wiki/NRP_Vasco_da_Gama_(F330)" title="NRP Vasco da Gama (F330)">bears his name</a>.
</p><p>The Portuguese government erected two navigational beacons, <b>Dias Cross</b> and <b>da Gama Cross</b>, to commemorate da Gama and <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> who were the first modern European explorers to reach the Cape of Good Hope. When lined up, these crosses point to Whittle Rock, a large, permanently submerged shipping hazard in <a href="/wiki/False_Bay" title="False Bay">False Bay</a>.
</p><p>South African musician <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Masekela" title="Hugh Masekela">Hugh Masekela</a> recorded an anti-colonialist song entitled "Colonial Man", which contains the lyrics "Vasco da Gama was no friend of mine", and another song entitled "Vasco da Gama (The Sailor Man)". Both songs were included in his 1976 album <i><a href="/wiki/Colonial_Man" title="Colonial Man">Colonial Man</a></i>.
</p><p>Vasco da Gama appears as an antagonist in the Indian film <i><a href="/wiki/Urumi_(film)" title="Urumi (film)">Urumi</a></i>. The film, directed by Santosh Sivan, depicts atrocities and progression to establish the Portuguese empire by da Gama in India.
</p><p>In March 2016, archaeologists working off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> identified a shipwreck believed to be that of the <i>Esmeralda</i> from da Gama's 1502–1503 fleet. The wreck was initially discovered in 1998. Later underwater excavations took place between 2013 and 2015 through a partnership between the Oman Ministry of Heritage and Culture and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Water_Recoveries" title="Blue Water Recoveries">Blue Water Recoveries</a> Ltd., a shipwreck recovery company. The vessel was identified through such artifacts as a "Portuguese coin minted for trade with India (one of only two coins of this type known to exist) and stone cannonballs engraved with what appear to be the initials of Vincente Sodré, da Gama's maternal uncle and the commander of the <i>Esmeralda</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">At this time in Portugal, there were only twelve counts, one count-bishop, two marquises and two dukes (Subrahmaynam, 1997, p. 281).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Subrahmanyam, 1997, p. 304.</span>
